25:T13b6,<entryFree id="n15393" key="رَزَقَهُ ٱللّٰهُ" type="main">

                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَزَقَهُ ٱللّٰهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">رَزُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Msb, TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رِزْقٌ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">رَزْقٌ</foreign>, (IB, K,) the latter being the proper inf. n., (K,) and the former a simple subst. but also used as an inf. n., (TA,) <hi rend="ital">God caused what is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِزْق</foreign> [q. v.] <hi rend="ital">to come to him:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">God gave him.</hi> (S, IB.) [The verb is doubly trans.: when the second objective complement is implied, the phrase generally means <hi rend="ital">God caused the means of subsistence to come to him;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">gave him, granted him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bestowed upon him, the means of subsistence;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">supplied, provided,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blessed, him therewith:</hi> when the second objective complement is expressed, this word is generally one signifying the means of subsistence or the like, property, or offspring.] One says also, <foreign lang="ar">رَزَقَ الطَّائِرُ فَرْخَهُ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">رَزُقَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَزْقٌ</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">The bird fed its young one.</hi>] (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَزَقَ الأَمِيرُ الجُنْدَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The commander gave their subsistence-money, pay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">allowances, to the army:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">رَزَقَ الجُنْدَ رَزْقَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He gave the army their subsistence-money,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">once:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">رُزِقُوا رَزْقَتَيْنِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">They were given their subsistence-money,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">twice.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence <foreign lang="ar">رُزِقَ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a place) <hi rend="ital">was rained upon.</hi>] Lebeed says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">رُزِقَتْ مَرَابِيعَ النُّجُومِ وَصَابَهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَدْقُ الرَّوَاعِدِ جَوْدُهَا وَرِهَامُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> meaning <foreign lang="ar">مُطِرَتْ</foreign>; (TA;) i. e. <hi rend="ital">They were rained upon with the rain of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَآء</foreign> [pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نَوْءٌ</foreign> q. v.] <hi rend="ital">of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيع</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and the rain of the thundering clouds fell upon them, the copious thereof and the drizzling and lasting thereof.</hi> (EM pp. 140 and 141.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">رَزَقَ فُلَانًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He thanked such a one; was thankful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grateful, to him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acknowledged his beneficence:</hi> of the dial. of Azd, (K,) i. e. Azd-Shanooah. (TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذٰلِكَ لَمَّا رَزَقْتَنِى</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">لَمَّا شَكَرْتَنِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I did that since,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">because, thou thankedst me</hi>]. (TA.) And hence, in the Kur [lvi. 81], <foreign lang="ar">وَتَجْعَلُونَ رِزْقَكُمْ أَنَّكُمْ تَكَذِّبُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And do ye make your thanking to be that ye disacknowledge</hi> the benefit received, as being from God?]; (K;) i. e., accord. to Ibn-'Arafeh, do ye, instead of acknowledging what God has bestowed upon you, and being thankful for it, attribute it to another than Him? or, accord. to Az and others, [as J also says in the S,] the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">تَجْعَلُونَ شَكْرَ رِزِقْكُمُ التَّكْذِيبَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">do ye make the thanking for your sustenance to be disacknowledgment?</hi>]: (TA:) and some read <foreign lang="ar">شَكْرَكُمْ</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">رِزْقَكُمْ</foreign>]. (Bd.)    </entryFree>26:T132b,<entryFree id="n15396" key="رِزْقٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رِزْقٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A thing whereby one profits,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from which one derives advantage;</hi> (S, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15396-1" target="مُرْتَزَقٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n15404"/></foreign>, (K, TA,) in the pass. form: (TA: [in the CK, erroneously, <foreign lang="ar">مُرْتَزِق</foreign>:]) and <hi rend="ital">a gift;</hi> and especially, of God: (S:) or [especially, and according to general usage,] the <hi rend="ital">means of subsistence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of the support and growth of the body, which God sends to</hi> [<hi rend="ital">mankind and other</hi>] <hi rend="ital">animals;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">sustenance, victuals, food,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">provisions;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a supply thereof from God:</hi>] but with the Moatezileh it means <hi rend="ital">a thing possessed and eaten by the deserving;</hi> so that it does not apply to what is unlawful: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَرْزَاقٌ</foreign>: (S, Msb, K:) and what are thus termed are of two kinds; <hi rend="ital">apparent,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">material,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">which are for the bodies, such as aliments;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">unapparent,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">intellectual,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">which are for the hearts and minds, such as the several sorts of knowledge and of science:</hi> (TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">رِزْقٌ</foreign> properly signifies <hi rend="ital">a portion, share,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lot;</hi> or particularly, <hi rend="ital">of something good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellent;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">حَظٌّ</foreign>: and is conventionally made to apply to <hi rend="ital">a thing by which an animal is enabled to profit:</hi> (Bd in ii. 2:) and [hence] it signifies also <hi rend="ital">a daily allowance of food</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like;</hi> and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15396-2" target="رِزْقَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n15398"/></foreign> of <pb n="1077"/> which the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">رِزَقٌ</foreign>: (TA:) [the <hi rend="ital">subsistencemoney, pay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">allowance,</hi> of a soldier; or] <hi rend="ital">what is given forth to the soldier at the commencement of every month,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">day by day:</hi> or, accord. to ElKarkhee, <foreign lang="ar">العَطَآءُ</foreign> is what is assigned to those who fight; and <foreign lang="ar">الرَّزْقُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">to the poor:</hi> (Mgh: [but see <foreign lang="ar">عَطَآءٌ</foreign>:]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15396-3" target="رَزَقَاتٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, pl. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15396-4" target="رَزَقَةٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, which is the inf. n. of unity of <foreign lang="ar">رَرَقَ</foreign>, signifies the <hi rend="ital">portions of subsistence-money, pay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">allowances,</hi> (syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَطْمَاع</foreign>,) of soldiers: (S, K:) one says, <foreign lang="ar">كَمْ رِزْقُكَ فِى الشَّهْرِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">How much is thy allowance of food,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">thy subsistence-money,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pay,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in the month?</hi> (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذُوا أَرْزَاقَهُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They took,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">received, their portions of subsistence-money,</hi> &amp;c.,] (S, Msb, K) is said of soldiers. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">الرِّزْقُ الحَسَنُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">A thing</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">provision</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that comes to one without toil in the seeking thereof:</hi> or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">a thing</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">provision</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that is found without one's looking,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">watching, for it, and without one's reckoning upon it, and without one's earning it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">labouring to earn it.</hi> (KT.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Rain</hi> (S, K) is sometimes thus called; as in the Kur xlv. 4 and li. 22: this being an amplification in language; as when one says, “ The dates are in the bottom of the well; ” meaning thereby “ the [water for] watering the palm-trees. ” (S.)    </entryFree>27:T593,<entryFree id="n15400" key="الرَّازِقُ" type="main">
